Peterson</strong> (<a href=\"https://twitter.com/jordanbpeterson\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">@jordanbpeterson</a>) has taught mythology to lawyers, doctors, and business people, consulted for the UN secretary-general, helped his clinical clients manage depression, obsessive-compulsive disorder, anxiety, and schizophrenia, served as an adviser to senior partners of major Canadian law firms, and lectured extensively in North America and Europe.</p> \n<p>With his students and colleagues at Harvard and the University of Toronto, Dr. Peterson has published more than one hundred scientific papers, transforming the modern understanding of personality, as his book <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Maps-Meaning-Architecture-Jordan-Peterson/dp/0415922224\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\"><em>Maps of Meaning: The Architecture of Belief</em></a> revolutionized the psychology of religion.</p> \n<p>His book <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/12-Rules-Life-Antidote-Chaos/dp/0345816021\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\"><em>12 Rules for Life: An Antidote to Chaos</em></a> was published in 2018 and has sold more than 4 million copies internationally. His latest book is <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Beyond-Order-More-Rules-Life/dp/0593084640\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\"><strong><em>Beyond Order: 12 More Rules for Life</em></strong></a>.</p> \n<p>Please enjoy! </p> \n<p><strong><em>Listen to the episode on <a href=\"https://podcasts.apple.com/us/podcast/502-jordan-peterson-on-rules-for-life-psychedelics/id863897795?i=1000511230875\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Apple Podcasts</a>, <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://open.spotify.com/episode/26FfERs6w1GD6B0VDVWnKe?si=WqZrX5aPSAmSjsM6zSvDYg\" target=\"_blank\">Spotify</a>, <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://overcast.fm/+KebvddEKc\" target=\"_blank\">Overcast</a>, <a rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://www.stitcher.com/podcast/the-tim-ferriss-show\" target=\"_blank\">Stitcher</a>, <a rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://castbox.fm/channel/id1059468?country=us\" target=\"_blank\">Castbox</a>, <a rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://podcasts.google.com/?feed=aHR0cHM6Ly9yc3MuYXJ0MTkuY29tL3RpbS1mZXJyaXNzLXNob3c&amp;ved=0CAAQ4aUDahcKEwjI_ezXzuDnAhUAAAAAHQAAAAAQAQ\" target=\"_blank\">Google Podcasts</a>, or on your favorite podcast platform.</em></strong> <em><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=C1sEHNw4UIg&amp;feature=youtu.be\" target=\"_blank\"><strong>Watch on YouTube here.</strong></a></em></p> \n<p><strong><em>Brought to you by <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"http://wealthfront.com/tim\" target=\"_blank\">Wealthfront</a> automated investing, <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"http://helixsleep.com/tim\" target=\"_blank\">Helix Sleep</a> premium mattresses, and <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"http://athleticgreens.com/tim\" data-type=\"URL\" target=\"_blank\">Athletic Greens</a> all-in-one nutritional supplement. [05:23]</li>\n <li>Early influential books that have stood the test of time for Jordan, and what listeners can expect to gain by delving into the list of books he recommends at his website. [08:57]</li>\n <li>On the Nietzschean idea of morality as cowardice, and what we might do to cultivate courage while keeping our more dangerous inclinations in check. [11:37]</li>\n <li>Drawing a distinction between thinking and paying attention as a way to gain insight during a conversation that may turn adversarial, and why resentment, for all its ugliness, can be a valuable consultant. [16:18]</li>\n <li>On finding meaning to make life’s suffering irrelevant (or at least non-corrupting), and Jordan’s thoughts about how this perspective informs his conservative leanings. [24:10]</li>\n <li>What does Jordan feel is the <em>right</em> way to constructively criticize a social institution? [29:30]</li>\n <li>Jordan weighs in on what he finds fascinating about psychology and the physiology of drug and alcohol use, and what he considers to be the “Pandora’s Box” of seeking religious experiences through psychedelics. [34:43]</li>\n <li>If the contents of this Pandora’s Box facilitate greater openness, when might this <em>not</em> be a good thing? How does Jordan define openness in this context, and how does it relate to Carl Jung’s warning to “beware of unearned wisdom?” [39:48]</li>\n <li>In what ways does Jordan believe the world is, as he puts it, “deeply strange?” How did his son once inexplicably illustrate the chaos and order of this strangeness from a child’s perspective? [45:24]</li>\n <li>Stoned apes, high flies, and the risk of ontological shock faced by people who pursue psychoactive experiences too casually. [51:00]</li>\n <li>What might the average person in the Western world, religious or not, gain by studying the Bible? [53:57]</li>\n <li>Jordan believes that ancient stories — as found in the Bible — carry kernels of wisdom that have been stripped of superfluousness over time. When writing a book, how does he try to convey his own messages in a way that will remain intact over time to serve further generations? [59:54]</li>\n <li>How writing a book can be the meaning an author needs to keep going, and why finishing it can counterintuitively be a source of devastation rather than elation. [1:02:25]</li>\n <li>What would Jordan recommend to someone seeking meaning if they have reached a high level of competence in a certain area? [1:03:30]</li>\n <li>Why is Jordan’s new book called <em>Beyond Order</em>? [1:05:23]</li>\n <li>Beyond sales, what would make Jordan consider <em>Beyond Order</em> a success? [00:00]</li>\n <li>Parting thoughts. [1:16:48]</li>\n</ul> \n<h3>PEOPLE MENTIONED</h3> \n<ul>\n <li><a href=\"https://www.ualberta.ca/research/research-support/post-doctoral-office/awards-funding/u-of-a-fellowships/about-grant-notley.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Grant Notley</a></li>\n <li><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ayn_Rand\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Ayn Rand</a></li>\n <li><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aldous_Huxley\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Aldous Huxley</a></li>\n <li><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_Orwell\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">George Orwell</a></li>\n <li><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aleksandr_Solzhenitsyn\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Aleksandr Solzhenitsyn</a></li>\n <li><a href=\"https://twitter.com/rachelnotley?lang=en\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Rachel Notley</a></li>\n <li><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fyodor_Dostoevsky\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Fyodor Dostoevsky</a></li>\n <li><a href=\"https://plato.stanford.edu/entries/nietzsche/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Friedrich Nietzsche</a></li>\n <li><a href=\"https://www.whitehouse.gov/about-the-white-house/presidents/abraham-lincoln/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Abraham Lincoln</a></li>\n <li><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oscar_Wilde\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Oscar Wilde</a></li>\n <li><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Viktor_Frankl\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Viktor Frankl</a></li>\n <li><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hunter_S._Thompson\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Hunter S. <figcaption>\n  Illustration via \n  <a href=\"http://99designs.com/tim\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">99designs</a>\n </figcaption>\n</figure> \n<blockquote class=\"wp-block-quote\">\n <p>“We really began to be tired of ourselves teaching this technology of inner awakening to the same people over and over. It’s like, how many times do you have to wake up in the morning? You’re awake. Do something.”</p>\n <cite>— Elizabeth Lesser</cite>\n</blockquote> \n<p><strong>Elizabeth Lesser</strong> (<a target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://twitter.com/ElizabethLesser\">@ElizabethLesser</a>) is a bestselling author and the co-founder of <a target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://www.eomega.org/\">Omega Institute</a>, the renowned conference and retreat center located in Rhinebeck, New York. Elizabeth’s first book, <a target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Seekers-previously-published-American-Spirituality/dp/0679783598\"><em>The Seeker’s Guide</em></a>, chronicles her years at Omega and distills lessons learned into a potent guide for growth and healing. Her <em>New York Times</em> bestselling book, <a target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Broken-Open-Difficult-Times-Help/dp/0375759913\"><em>Broken Open: How Difficult Times Can Help Us Grow</em></a>, has sold almost 500,000 copies and has been translated into 20 languages. Her third book, <a target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Marrow-Love-Loss-What-Matters/dp/006236765X\"><em>Marrow</em></a><em>, </em>chronicles the journey Elizabeth and her younger sister went through when Elizabeth was the donor for her sister’s bone marrow transplant. Her newest book, <a target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Cassandra-Speaks-Women-Storytellers-Changes/dp/0062887181\"><strong><em>Cassandra Speaks: When Women Are the Storytellers, the Human Story Changes</em></strong></a>, reveals how humanity has outgrown its origin tales and hero myths. Elizabeth has given two popular TED talks and is one of Oprah Winfrey’s Supersoul 100, a collection of a hundred leaders who are using their voices and talent to elevate humanity.</p> \n<p>She co-founded Omega Institute in 1977—a time when a variety of fresh ideas were sprouting in American culture. Since then, the Institute has been at the forefront of holistic education, offering workshops and conferences in integrative medicine, meditation and yoga, cross-cultural arts and creativity, ecumenical spirituality, and social change. Each year close to 30,000 people participate in Omega’s programs on its campus, and more than a million people visit its website for online learning.</p> \n<p>Please enjoy! </p> \n<p><em>Note from the editor: Timestamps will be added shortly. </em></p> \n<ul>\n <li>Why visiting Omega Institute might feel a little like starring in your own Disney film.</li>\n <li>Who is Pir Vilayat Inayat Khan?</li>\n <li>Coming from an atheistic background, how did Elizabeth find herself on a spiritual path when she first encountered Pir Vilayat Inayat Khan, and what did he help her discover?</li>\n <li>What did the prototype look like for Omega Institute, and how did Elizabeth and her co-founders decide on what to include versus exclude?</li>\n <li>What issues made the early Omega Institute pioneers rethink their intention of living communally?</li>\n <li>How was the curriculum safely and legally aligned with the tagline of “awakening the best in the human spirit” during this time, and how were teachers selected?</li>\n <li>On the exploration of ecumenical traditions and innervism.</li>\n <li>What is <em>the movement from me to we</em>?</li>\n <li>How would Elizabeth define “spiritual” — or does she prefer another term?</li>\n <li>Elizabeth talks about sharing a “soul marrow transplant” with her sister Maggie, and how she discovered a particularly poignant needlepoint slogan after Maggie’s death that she’s adapted to her own meditation: “Do no harm and take no shit.”</li>\n <li>What is Authenticity Deficit Disorder?</li>\n <li>In my own experience, it’s not always an answer that helps us unburden ourselves of what Rumi called an open secret, but the act of asking. Does Elizabeth agree?</li>\n <li>Recommendations for people going through the grieving process — especially in a culture that doesn’t really afford us time to mourn.</li>\n <li>The importance of, as Henk Kraaijenhof has said, doing as little as needed, not as much as possible.</li>\n <li>What is the origin story of Elizabeth’s latest book, <em>Cassandra Speaks: When Women Are the Storytellers, the Human Story Changes</em>?</li>\n <li>Does Elizabeth believe an impulse toward aggression is inevitable in women who acquire power? If so, can it be mitigated to avoid the abuses exercised by many men in power? Why do people in power tend more toward the fight or flight school of thought over tend and befriend?</li>\n <li>What impact does Elizabeth hope to have with <em>Cassandra Speaks</em>? How does she believe that full-hearted fatherhood might save the world?</li>\n <li>What would Elizabeth’s billboard say?</li>\n <li>Parting thoughts.</li>\n</ul> \n<h3><strong>PEOPLE href=\"https://twitter.com/WalterIsaacson/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">@WalterIsaacson</a>) is a professor of history at Tulane, has been CEO of the Aspen Institute, chair of CNN, and editor of <em>Time</em>. He is the author of <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Leonardo-Vinci-Walter-Isaacson/dp/1501139150\" target=\"_blank\"><em>Leonardo da Vinci</em></a>; <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Innovators-Hackers-Geniuses-Created-Revolution/dp/147670869X\" target=\"_blank\"><em>The Innovators</em></a>; <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Steve-Jobs-Walter-Isaacson/dp/1451648537\" target=\"_blank\"><em>Steve Jobs</em></a>; <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Einstein-Life-Universe-Walter-Isaacson/dp/0743264738\" target=\"_blank\"><em>Einstein: His Life and Universe</em></a>; <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Benjamin-Franklin-American-Walter-Isaacson-dp-0684807610/dp/0684807610\" target=\"_blank\"><em>Benjamin Franklin: An American Life</em></a>; and <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Kissinger-Biography-Walter-Isaacson/dp/0671663232\" target=\"_blank\"><em>Kissinger: A Biography</em></a>. He is co-author of <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Wise-Men-Friends-World-They-ebook/dp/B00768DB2S\" target=\"_blank\"><em>The Wise Men: Six Friends and the World They Made</em></a>.</p> \n<p>His new book is <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Code-Breaker-Jennifer-Doudna-Editing/dp/1982115858\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\"><strong><em>The Code Breaker: Jennifer Doudna, Gene Editing, and the Future of the Human Race</em></strong></a>.</p> \n<p>You can find our first conversation from 2017 at <a href=\"https://tim.blog/2017/10/14/walter-isaacson/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">tim.blog/walter</a>.</p> \n<p>Please enjoy! What other projects has he similarly set aside? [07:23]</li>\n <li>Why did Walter add the job of college professor to what most mere mortals would consider an already overflowing schedule? [09:53]</li>\n <li>What makes home <em>home</em>? [11:42]</li>\n <li>What is CRISPR — who developed it, how has it been used so far, and what is its potential? [15:14]</li>\n <li>How did <em>The Double Helix</em> by James Watson influence a curious young Walter, and why did he choose Jennifer Doudna to be the protagonist of his latest book? [18:52]</li>\n <li>With fallible human motivations driving the use of this technology and the unintended consequences that are bound to result, What might a CRISPR-edited world look like — for better or worse? [22:09]</li>\n <li>How is CRISPR technology applied to adults, and what implications does this have, for instance, for competitive athletics and anti-doping efforts? [27:25]</li>\n <li>Walter riffs on innovation revolutions surrounding the three fundamental kernels of our existence: the atom, the bit, and the gene, and how he hopes <em>The Code Breaker</em> might galvanize future generations of scientists and scientific thinkers in the same way he and Jennifer Doudna were inspired by <em>The Double Helix</em>. [29:42]</li>\n <li>What does the education look like for someone who wants to better understand the molecule as the new microchip? [35:19]</li>\n <li>In a field with no shortage of legitimate geniuses, what makes Jennifer Doudna special? How was she able to work out a puzzle that had, until that point, eluded the efforts of every other scientist who tried? Was it just a matter of asking better questions? [39:47]</li>\n <li>As a biographer of many fascinating minds, with whom does Walter think Jennifer Doudna most closely compares? [46:53]</li>\n <li>How 19th-century computer pioneer Ada Lovelace and 20th-century computer scientist Alan Turing came to different conclusions about questions we may not even be able to answer in the 21st century. [48:57]</li>\n <li>Does Walter believe there’s a necessary seeking of wonder or awe — a motivation — behind the breed of curiosity shared by Lovelace, Doudna, and Franklin? [52:32]</li>\n <li>When science makes the leap from curiosity-driven discovery to practical application, a race to get credit and funding for related discoveries generally follows. What did this competition look like for Jennifer Doudna and partner Emmanuelle Charpentier when they realized that CRISPR could ignite a scientific revolution, and against whom did they compete? What are the pros and cons of such competition, and what prizes <em>really</em> motivate the participants? [55:12]</li>\n <li>What insights, counterintuitive wisdom, and memorable points about pandemic life past and present have been made clear to Walter by the work of fellow author (and, coincidentally, neighbor!) John Barry, who wrote <em>The Great Influenza: The Epic Story of the Deadliest Plague in History</em>? [1:02:59]</li>\n <li>Like Albert Hoffman, Robert Oppenheimer, and Victor Frankenstein, scientists sometimes have to face the misapplications of (and the monsters created by) their discoveries. After a nightmare about how Hitler might have abused CRISPR technology, how has Jennifer Doudna been reckoning with the moral implications of her own work? [1:05:20]</li>\n <li>Is it possible to create globally enforceable guard rails for how CRISPR technology should be used, or is it too late now that Pandora’s box has been opened? What makes its regulation more tricky than other potentially destructive technologies, like nuclear weapons? [1:08:11]</li>\n <li>Is there any aspect of <em>The Code Breaker</em> that Walter worries some people might misinterpret or miss entirely? [1:10:35]</li>\n <li>Why it might finally be philosophy’s time to shine as a practical skill set, and responsibly asking “why not?” is just as important as asking “why?” [1:12:59]</li>\n <li>Parting thoughts. [1:17:25]</li>\n</ul> \n<h3>PEOPLE MENTIONED</h3> \n<ul>\n <li><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leonardo_da_Vinci\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Leonardo da Vinci</a></li>\n e.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/timferriss/~4/YbxsRHpbY2c":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn13@2020_1/2021/04/03/04-49-51-653_1a75a6583365d775.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1617425326499},{"createdTime":"2021-04-03 12:48:46","updatedTime":"2021-04-03 12:48:46","title":"Some Thoughts on For-Profit Psychedelic Startups and Companies","link":"https://tim.blog/?p=55063","description":"\n<figure class=\"wp-block-image size-large\"><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"600\" height=\"600\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/tim.blog/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/Lewis-Minor-Photo.jpg?resize=600%2C600&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" class=\"wp-image-55066\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/tim.blog/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/Lewis-Minor-Photo.jpg?resize=1024%2C1024&#38;ssl=1 1024w, https://i2.wp.com/tim.blog/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/Lewis-Minor-Photo.jpg?resize=768%2C768&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i2.wp.com/tim.blog/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/Lewis-Minor-Photo.jpg?w=1800&#38;ssl=1 1800w, https://i2.wp.com/tim.blog/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/Lewis-Minor-Photo.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 767px) 90vw, 600px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><figcaption>Credit: <a href=\"https://flickr.com/photos/31284576@N06/5036712014/in/photolist-8F5t1j-95nTrL-rqLAHi-Kk9GHy-brcZGM-NFRP51-R9y5Su-cFRqZj-232nL6x-2kaaYWk-6y5iw5-2cbccna-sE2qVL-phRWgT-rgsAx2-skhAfL-FqKj5t-zwYKfJ-27PvP35-aFB2Ba-2gMD6e6-q7baZy-2iNzhgg-VEPP3f-25SP7pi-FsUFhQ-BrAoVe-5DfGXv-boE3y-oVCWup-dLmRw7-9kJxyv-fKuazu-ec8fj8-snzzza-aFDcrg-4LJRt4-s5uE6-7jFqA3-M91C-BeDti6-bZvY7w-qzk2Z3-ELYThj-YfDRD4-bnFUG4-9VAoaM-fTr2eB-8ddtDt-bf3TAn\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Lewis Minor</a></figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>This week has been a fascinating firestorm for me.&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Part of the excitement came after <a href=\"https://twitter.com/tferriss/status/1366887907248771077\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">a series of tweets</a> I published about some of the concerns I have as psychedelic medicine makes the leap from research to for-profit startups and companies. Here is what I wrote:<br><br>“I am very concerned by the patent land grab warming up in the for-profit psychedelic world. Is anyone working on an IP Defense Fund—or coalition of pro-bono lawyers—of some type to file USPTO objections/comments, etc. when companies attempt to secure broad patents that could hinder scientific research, reasonable competition (i.e., for &#8220;scale&#8221; and wide accessibility, we need competition to help drive costs down), and so on? Who are the smartest people thinking about this?<br>cc <a href=\"https://twitter.com/michaelpollan\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">@michaelpollan</a>, <a href=\"https://twitter.com/Drug_Researcher\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">@Drug_Researcher</a>, <a href=\"https://twitter.com/RickDoblin\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">@RickDoblin</a>, <a href=\"https://twitter.com/RCarhartHarris\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">@RCarhartHarris</a>”</p>\n\n\n\n<p>[If helpful, <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://twitter.com/tferriss/status/1366887907248771077\" target=\"_blank\">here is the link to the actual thread on Twitter</a>.]<br><br>In this post, I&#8217;ll describe a few noteworthy tweets, then I&#8217;ll focus on one particular response I received, as it helps us unpack a lot.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>First, <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://tim.blog/2020/06/11/rick-doblin/\" target=\"_blank\">Rick Doblin</a> of The Multidisciplinary Association for Psychedelic Studies (MAPS) replied with the below, which offers great food for thought. It demonstrates how non-profits and drug development can coexist with innovative business models. It also demonstrates how a profit-first model is NOT always necessary for attracting excellent talent to work on tough problems:</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-embed is-type-rich is-provider-twitter wp-block-embed-twitter\"><div class=\"wp-block-embed__wrapper\">\n<blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\"><p lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\"><a href=\"https://twitter.com/tferriss?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">@tferriss</a>: <a href=\"https://twitter.com/MAPS?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">@MAPS</a> has recently engaged patent attorneys to assist in strengthening our anti-patent strategy for uses of MDMA, and to prepare easily accessible information for patent examiners so patents will not be issued in the first place. <a href=\"https://t.co/ndcAELkDi4\">pic.twitter.com/ndcAELkDi4</a></p>&#8212; Rick Doblin, MAPS (@RickDoblin) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/RickDoblin/status/1367288770697916418?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">March 4, 2021</a></blockquote><script async src=\"https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script>\n</div></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>Several responses endorsed the <strong><a href=\"https://www.usonainstitute.org/about/\">Usona Institute</a></strong> &#8212; a 501(c)(3) non-profit dedicated to both research and production of psilocybin, <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://pubs.acs.org/doi/10.1021/acsomega.0c05099\" target=\"_blank\">5-MeO-DMT</a>, and other psychedelic medicines &#8212; which has made commitments to Open Science. I have many friends who have supported Usona after due diligence. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>And now to the tweet that will be our jumping-off point for many topics&#8230; <br><br>One response that got quite a bit of attention was from Christian Angermeyer, who has co-funded and co-founded two notable for-profit companies in the space, <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://compasspathways.com/\" target=\"_blank\">Compass Pathways</a> and <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://www.atai.life/\" target=\"_blank\">ATAI Life Sciences</a>, respectively. <br><br>Before we go further, I want to note that I like Christian and have also moderated panels involving him (e.g., <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://tim.blog/2019/07/15/psychedelics-microdosing-mind-enhancing-methods/\" target=\"_blank\">the psychedelic science panel at Milken Institute Global Conference 2019</a>, which I think is the best 101 overview I’ve ever been a part of), where I’ve always found his perspectives valuable.&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<p>He is sincere in his goal to help millions with access to psychedelics, and here is his response to my thread (in case easier, <a href=\"https://149346886.v2.pressablecdn.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/Screen-Shot-2021-03-05-at-5.16.45-PM.png\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">screenshot is here</a>):</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-embed is-type-rich is-provider-twitter wp-block-embed-twitter\"><div class=\"wp-block-embed__wrapper\">\n<blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\"><p lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\">Tim, I am a huge fan, but here is why you are wrong <a href=\"https://twitter.com/michaelpollan?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">@michaelpollan</a> <a href=\"https://twitter.com/RickDoblin?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">@RickDoblin</a> <a href=\"https://twitter.com/RCarhartHarris?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">@RCarhartHarris</a> <a href=\"https://t.co/VIhdGeHdG8\">pic.twitter.com/VIhdGeHdG8</a></p>&#8212; Christian Angermayer (@C_Angermayer) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/C_Angermayer/status/1366904464616140800?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">March 3, 2021</a></blockquote><script async src=\"https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script>\n</div></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>I planned on responding on Twitter, but it got long and Twitter wouldn’t let me. I also realized that the points, problems, and questions are relevant to nearly anyone starting or working for a for-profit company in the psychedelic space.<br><br>For those reasons and more, I decided to turn my response into a blog post.<br><br>Here it is…<br><br>###<br><br>Thank you for the response, Christian. I agree with nearly everything in your response and appreciate the dialogue.<br><br>That said, I don’t think it directly addresses my concerns. To further the conversation, please allow me to highlight and clarify a few things:</p>\n\n\n\n<p><strong>1. </strong>I’m not anti-profit. I’m an early investor or advisor in 50+ companies that have created hundreds of billions of dollars of market cap (e.g., Shopify, Uber, Facebook, Twitter, Alibaba) and raised tens of billions of dollars in funding. I understand how important intellectual property (IP) can be and how critical it is to have financially sustainable models for scaling. 100% agreed there. For-profit structures, and markets in general, are excellent mechanisms for innovation and solving challenging problems.</p>\n\n\n\n<p><strong>2. </strong>Regarding my donations of “a few million dollars,” which seemed to be considered trivial—I think it’s worth noting that I began funding studies in psychedelic science circa late 2015, and I was a founding funder of the first dedicated research center in the world (<a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://www.imperial.ac.uk/psychedelic-research-centre/\" target=\"_blank\">Imperial College</a>) and the first in the US (<a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://hopkinspsychedelic.org/\" target=\"_blank\">Johns Hopkins</a>). I believe these and other “seed investments” have had large compounding effects, including cultural and institutional domino effects on an international scale. I judge my investments and philanthropy based on outcomes, not the size of my inputs. <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://tim.blog/2007/10/04/karmic-capitalist-should-i-wait-until-im-rich-to-give/\" target=\"_blank\">Little amounts can do a lot when put in early</a>. Of course, I completely agree that large amounts of capital are helpful for scaling access. <br><br><strong>Related to science — would you be willing to allow scientists who have signed deals with Compass or ATAI to share their agreements publicly (i.e., waive confidentiality clauses)? I believe that would quell some of the concerns among psychedelic advocates. If not, why not?</strong></p>\n\n\n\n<p>Of course, I realize that this would be unusual and not without challenges, but it might be a creative example of how companies can reassure the public that they are, net-net, contributing to, and not detracting from or disabling, the ecosystem.&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<p><strong>&#160;3.</strong> <strong>You wrote that I’m “wrong” and “incredibly misguided” on the topic of IP. Can you please help me understand how I’m wrong and misguided? I’m always game to learn, but I could use more specifics.</strong></p>\n\n\n\n<p>As I stated in my initial tweet thread, I think it’s worth examining—and possibly pushing back on—“broad patents that could hinder scientific research, reasonable competition (i.e., for ‘scale’ and wide accessibility, we need competition to help drive costs down), and so on.” This also applies to anything in the public domain that should remain in the public domain. Please note that I didn’t mention specific companies, but since you engaged&#8230;</p>\n\n\n\n<p><strong>Do you disagree? Do you think a monopoly/duopoly of any type (Compass or ATAI or otherwise), patents on basic elements of the psychedelic experience, or patents covering dozens of possible conditions that might be treatable (some of which are being treated/researched at universities) would be good for the ecosystem, for innovation, or for ensuring affordable pricing?</strong></p>\n\n\n\n<p>I ask these things AS A CHEERLEADER. I WANT Compass and ATAI to succeed in helping many millions of people! I’ve met you, as well as the founders of Compass, and I believe you all to be good people. I really mean it. I believe that you all want to change the world for the better, and this field needs well-capitalized teams who can execute.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Compass and other for-profit companies have the potential to do a ton of good in the world. I also think that the nature and incentives of capitalism can breed strategies that are very bad for innovation, and we need individuals, groups, and third-party organizations to watch for them and mitigate them. Even the best of intentions can warp when they collide with the harsh realities of business.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>None of this is Compass- or ATAI-specific. It applies to every startup and company in the space.&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<p>For-profit ventures have a critical role to play in the expansion of psychedelic medicine, but for-profit ventures don’t get a free pass. They can also cause harm, and they often do. There will be compelling temptations to make unethical decisions, pursue unfair anti-competitive practices (e.g., patenting “inventions” that aren’t inventions), generate revenue without adding value (e.g., IP trolling), charge as much as possible (e.g., NYT &#8211; “<a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2015/09/21/business/a-huge-overnight-increase-in-a-drugs-price-raises-protests.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Drug Goes From $13.50 a Tablet to $750, Overnight</a>“), and treat the psychedelic landscape as a winner-take-all or zero-sum game. “Disruption” can be white hat or black hat; “scaling” can be done with net-gain or net-loss to an ecosystem.<br><br>There are bad actors and mercenaries in every industry. But here’s the part that people forget: even if the founders of a company rival Mother Theresa in their moral character and strength, that isn’t enough. Leadership changes, incentives change, power dynamics change, and all situations change (Suggested reading: <a href=\"https://hereandnowstudios.com/we-will-call-it-pala\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">We Will Call It Pala</a>). That’s why both internal guardrails and external watchdogs are important. Once again, even the purest of intentions can warp when they collide with the harsh realities of business. I’ve seen it.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>In the end, the people who would most suffer as a result of the possible problems I’ve outlined are the millions of people who most need psychedelic medicine. That is why I’m taking the time to write and publish my concerns.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Once again, thank you for the dialogue, <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://twitter.com/C_Angermayer/status/1366904464616140800\" target=\"_blank\">Christian</a>. I greatly appreciate it, and I greatly appreciate your mission to help as many people as possible. I look forward to your thoughts.<br><br>Most sincerely,</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Tim<br><br><strong>[UPDATE: Christian posted his response <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/pulse/open-letter-tim-ferriss-value-patents-psychedelic-angermayer?trk=public_profile_article_view\" target=\"_blank\">here on LinkedIn</a>, and <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://www.vice.com/en/article/3an9eb/investors-are-debating-who-should-own-the-future-of-psychedelics\" target=\"_blank\"><em>VICE</em> publishe</a><a href=\"https://www.vice.com/en/article/3an9eb/investors-are-debating-who-should-own-the-future-of-psychedelics\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">d</a><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://www.vice.com/en/article/3an9eb/investors-are-debating-who-should-own-the-future-of-psychedelics\" target=\"_blank\"> a follow-up article discussing their evaluation of the exchange</a>.]</strong></p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/timferriss?a=z6UzdTmtQMI:_JmvWSQtzv4:V_sGLiPBpWU\"><img \n<blockquote class=\"wp-block-quote\">\n <p>“We wanted digital nations but we got digital nationalism.”</p>\n <cite>— Vitalik Buterin</cite>\n</blockquote> \n<p><strong>Vitalik Buterin</strong> (@<a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://twitter.com/VitalikButerin\" target=\"_blank\">VitalikButerin</a>) is the creator of <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://ethereum.org/en/\" target=\"_blank\">Ethereum</a>. He first discovered blockchain and cryptocurrency technologies through Bitcoin in 2011 and was immediately excited by the technology and its potential. He co-founded <em>Bitcoin Magazine</em> in September 2011, and after two and a half years of looking at what the existing blockchain technology and applications had to offer, wrote the Ethereum white paper in November of 2013. He now leads Ethereum’s research team, working on future versions of the Ethereum protocol. In 2014, Vitalik was a recipient of the two-year Thiel Fellowship, tech billionaire Peter Thiel’s project that awards $100,000 to 20 promising innovators under 20 so they can pursue their inventions in lieu of a post-secondary institution path. You can find his website at <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"http://vitalik.ca\" target=\"_blank\">Vitalik.ca</a>.</p> \n<p><strong>Naval Ravikant</strong> (<a href=\"http://twitter.com/naval\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">@naval</a>) is the co-founder and chairman of <a href=\"https://angel.co/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">AngelList</a>. He is an angel investor and has invested in more than 100 companies, including many mega-successes, such as Twitter, Uber, Notion, Opendoor, Postmates, and Wish. You can subscribe to <a href=\"https://nav.al/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Naval</a>, his podcast on wealth and happiness, on <a href=\"https://podcasts.apple.com/us/podcast/naval/id1454097755\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Apple Podcasts</a>, <a href=\"https://open.spotify.com/show/7qZAVw03FuurfYnWIWwkHY\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Spotify</a>, <a href=\"https://overcast.fm/itunes1454097755/naval\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Overcast</a>, or wherever you get your podcasts. You can also find his blog at <a href=\"https://nav.al/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">nav.al</a>.</p> \n<p>Please enjoy! </p> \n<p><strong><em>Listen to the episode on <a href=\"https://podcasts.apple.com/us/podcast/504-vitalik-buterin-creator-ethereum-on-understanding/id863897795?i=1000512237199\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Apple Podcasts</a>, <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://open.spotify.com/episode/5fuiS0ZmMxuUp7kpbO0M8J?si=jJWWECeuQeeWMwIYw7xbSg\" target=\"_blank\">Spotify</a>, <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://overcast.fm/+KebupuJGQ\" target=\"_blank\">Overcast</a>, <a rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://www.stitcher.com/podcast/the-tim-ferriss-show\" target=\"_blank\">Stitcher</a>, <a rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://castbox.fm/channel/id1059468?country=us\" target=\"_blank\">Castbox</a>, <a rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://podcasts.google.com/?feed=aHR0cHM6Ly9yc3MuYXJ0MTkuY29tL3RpbS1mZXJyaXNzLXNob3c&amp;ved=0CAAQ4aUDahcKEwjI_ezXzuDnAhUAAAAAHQAAAAAQAQ\" target=\"_blank\">Google Podcasts</a>, or on your favorite podcast platform.</em></strong> </p> \n<p><b style=\"font-style: italic;\">Brought to you by </b><strong style=\"font-style: italic; Illustration via \n  <a href=\"http://99designs.com/tim\">99designs</a>\n </figcaption>\n</figure> \n<blockquote class=\"wp-block-quote\">\n <p>“Resistance with a capital R, that force of self-sabotage, will try to stop you as a writer or an artist or anybody from achieving your best work, from following your calling, will try to distract you, undermine your self-confidence, make you procrastinate, make you quit, make you give into fear, or, on the other hand, make you such a perfectionist that you spend all day on one paragraph and you accomplish nothing. The concept of little successes, or of a routine, is to help you overcome that Resistance.”</p>\n <cite>— Steven Pressfield</cite>\n</blockquote> \n<p><strong>Steven Pressfield</strong> (<a href=\"https://twitter.com/SPressfield\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">@SPressfield</a>), a former Marine and graduate of Duke University, became an overnight success as a writer after 30 years of abject failure. Identifying the omnipresence of “Resistance,” the interior force of self-sabotage he described in <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/War-Art-Through-Creative-Battles/dp/1936891026\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\"><em>The War of Art</em></a>, has saved his own artistic life and has helped many others struggling to find their creative calling. Steven’s novels of the ancient world, including the nonfiction <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Warrior-Ethos-Steven-Pressfield/dp/193689100X\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\"><em>The Warrior Ethos</em></a>, are required reading at West Point, Annapolis, and in the Marine Corps. He lives in Los Angeles.</p> \n<p>His new book is <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Man-at-Arms-Novel/dp/0393540979\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\"><strong><em>A Man at Arms</em></strong></a>, an epic saga about a reluctant hero, the Roman Empire, and the rise of a new faith.</p> \n<p>Please enjoy! </p> \n<p><strong><em>Listen to the episode on <a href=\"https://podcasts.apple.com/us/podcast/501-steven-pressfield-on-artists-journey-wisdom-little/id863897795?i=1000510784746\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Apple Podcasts</a>, <a href=\"https://open.spotify.com/episode/3DoraojWu3hVKgCXQrZajk?si=knhhSjxtSyiH5WTyarMlWA\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Spotify</a>, <a href=\"https://overcast.fm/+KebvKfCQA\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Overcast</a>, <a rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://www.stitcher.com/podcast/the-tim-ferriss-show\" target=\"_blank\">Stitcher</a>, <a rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://castbox.fm/channel/id1059468?country=us\" target=\"_blank\">Castbox</a>, <a rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://podcasts.google.com/?feed=aHR0cHM6Ly9yc3MuYXJ0MTkuY29tL3RpbS1mZXJyaXNzLXNob3c&amp;ved=0CAAQ4aUDahcKEwjI_ezXzuDnAhUAAAAAHQAAAAAQAQ\" target=\"_blank\">Google Podcasts</a>, or on your favorite podcast platform.</em></strong> </p> \n<p><strong><em>Brought to you by <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"http://tonal.com\" target=\"_blank\">Tonal</a> smart home gym; <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"http://linkedin.com/navigator\" target=\"_blank\">LinkedIn Sales Navigator</a>, the best version of LinkedIn for sales professionals; and <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"http://athleticgreens.com/tim\" data-type=\"URL\" target=\"_blank\">Athletic Greens</a> all-in-one nutritional supplement. href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Kite-Runner-Khaled-Hosseini/dp/159463193X/?dchild=1&amp;keywords=The+Kite+Runner&amp;qid=1614354294&amp;sr=8-1&amp;linkCode=ll1&amp;linkId=22ac8571964db8fa00f441d588a2c390&amp;language=en_US&amp;ref_=as_li_ss_tl\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">The Kite Runner by Khaled Hosseini</a></li>\n <li><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Tribe-Mentors-Short-Advice-World/dp/1328994961/?dchild=1&amp;keywords=tribe+of+mentors&amp;qid=1614354648&amp;sr=8-1&amp;linkCode=ll1&amp;linkId=a3e281bfa614541193be4297a3771045&amp;language=en_US&amp;ref_=as_li_ss_tl\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Tribe of Mentors: Short Life Advice from the Best in the World by Tim Ferriss</a></li>\n</ul> \n<h3>SHOW NOTES</h3> \n<ul>\n <li>During tough times, Steven lived behind a house for $15 a month and befriended a backwoods cat. How did this cat become his role model, and what circumstances led to their friendship? [07:27]</li>\n <li>Steven’s theory about halfway houses and the people you’ll find there (which for a time included him). [14:21]</li>\n <li>From a resume more eclectic than most, what job stands out as being especially formative for Steven’s eventual pivot to writer? [15:55]</li>\n <li>Common examples of Steven’s self-sabotage in the working world, and how a caring mentor helped him up and shook him out of this destructive pattern. [18:18]</li>\n <li>After 30 years of what Steven calls “abject failure,” Steven published his first novel when he was in his early 50s. Where did he pick up his wordsmithing skills, and how did make the transition from blue-collar truck driver to successful novelist? [23:11]</li>\n <li>What did Steven pick up from his time as a copywriter in the world of advertising? [26:25]</li>\n <li>How does the hero’s journey, as coined by Joseph Campbell, differ from what Steven considers to be the artist’s journey? [31:39]</li>\n <li>During his own hero’s journey, what did Steven’s refusal of the call look like compared to that of other notable figures from ancient and modern mythology? [37:16]</li>\n <li>How did Steven go from a refusal of the call that ended in an act of self-destruction and an unfinished novel to becoming a prolific writer? [41:07]</li>\n <li>Finishing a first novel is a major feat, but getting it published is another thing altogether. How did he make it happen? Like most modern literary adventures, there’s a detour through Hollywood. [43:52]</li>\n <li>How Steven’s morning routine gives him the momentum to write with what his friend Randy calls a “little successes” approach. [50:33]</li>\n <li>What does Steven’s exercise routine look like? [53:22]</li>\n <li>The writing process that works well for Joyce Carol Oates probably wouldn’t work at all for Steven. How should someone think about developing a routine for <em>their own</em> creative process? [54:15]</li>\n <li>Recommended books on the writing process — including one that integrates the editor’s mindset to keep things on track. [1:00:43]</li>\n <li>Steven’s advice for overcoming “Resistance with a capital R” when we feel like anything we create today will never match (let alone exceed) what we created yesterday. [1:05:24]</li>\n <li>Why does Steven believe Resistance with a capital R exists? What purpose could it possibly serve? [1:10:11]</li>\n <li>What is a shadow career, and what’s Steven’s advice to someone who finds themselves in one (and is willing to acknowledge it)? [1:15:43]</li>\n <li>What compelled Steven to write his latest work of historical fiction, <em>A Man at Arms</em>? For that matter, what compels Steven to write fiction? [1:23:10]</li>\n <li>What distinguishes the stories that come fast and easy from the hard slogs, and what might I gain from testing the waters of fiction writing? [1:28:13]</li>\n <li>Fear-setting from an Israeli fighter pilot’s perspective. [1:32:59]</li>\n <li>What is the yetzer hara? [1:34:22]</li>\n <li>How should I best prepare to “go big” as an aspiring fiction writer? [1:37:36]</li>\n <li>What would Steven’s billboard say? [1:44:25]</li>\n <li>Parting thoughts. [1:46:07]</li>\n</ul> \n<h3>PEOPLE MENTIONED</h3> \n<ul>\n <li><a href=\"https://www.poetryfoundation.org/poets/mary-oliver\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Mary Oliver</a></li>\n class=\"wp-block-quote\">\n <p>“I wanted to do research that then leapt off the page and became tools that would enter people’s lives and make a meaningful difference to them.”</p>\n <cite>— Dr. Adam Gazzaley</cite>\n</blockquote> \n<p><strong>Adam Gazzaley, MD, PhD</strong> (<a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://twitter.com/adamgazz\" target=\"_blank\">@adamgazz</a>)<strong>,</strong> is the David Dolby Distinguished Professor of Neurology, Physiology, and Psychiatry at the University of California, San Francisco, and the founder and executive director of <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://neuroscape.ucsf.edu/\" target=\"_blank\"><strong>Neuroscape</strong></a>, a translational neuroscience center engaged in technology development and scientific research of novel brain assessments and optimization tools. Adam is co-founder and chief science advisor of Akili Interactive, Sensync, and JAZZ Venture Partners. He has been a scientific adviser for more than a dozen technology companies, including Apple, GE, Nielsen, and Deloitte.</p> \n<p>Adam has filed multiple patents—notably his invention of <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://www.ucsf.edu/news/2020/06/417841/fda-approves-video-game-based-ucsf-brain-research-adhd-therapy-kids\" target=\"_blank\">the first video game cleared by the FDA</a>—authored more than 150 scientific articles, and delivered over 675 invited presentations around the world. He wrote and hosted the nationally televised PBS special <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://www.amazon.com/dp/B00BNBJ0LA/?linkCode=ll1&amp;linkId=5acb0e850d075ebf8e89ec3f8bc70be6&amp;language=en_US&amp;ref_=as_li_ss_tl\" target=\"_blank\"><em>The Distracted Mind with Dr. Adam Gazzaley</em></a> and co-authored <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Distracted-Mind-Ancient-Brains-High-Tech-ebook/dp/B08BSYX83P\" target=\"_blank\"><em>The Distracted Mind: Ancient Brains in a High-Tech World</em></a>, winner of the 2017 PROSE Award. Adam has received many awards and honors, including the 2015 Society for Neuroscience Science Educator Award and the 2020 Global Gaming Citizen honor.</p> \n<p>Visit&nbsp;<a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://neuroscape.ucsf.edu/psychedelics/\" target=\"_blank\">this page</a>&nbsp;to learn more about the&nbsp;<a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://neuroscape.ucsf.edu/psychedelics/\" target=\"_blank\"><strong>Neuroscape Psychedelic Division</strong></a>, which is dedicated to advancing the field of psychedelic science and medicine through multi-level research covering basic to translational to clinical science.</p> \n<p>Please enjoy!</p> \n<p><strong><em>Listen to the episode on <a href=\"https://podcasts.apple.com/us/podcast/507-dr-adam-gazzaley-ucsf-brain-optimization-future/id863897795?i=1000515030655\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Apple Podcasts</a>, <a Who Set Up the $85 Million Pineapple Fund | Bitcoin Magazine</a></li>\n</ul> \n<h3>SHOW NOTES</h3> \n<ul>\n <li>How NeuroRacer, the game Adam helped develop, helps older adults regain the cognitive function they had in their 20s, and why its featured spot as the cover story of <em>Nature</em> made Adam feel like he’d won a Grammy. [06:46]</li>\n <li>What has motivated Adam to pursue groundbreaking scientific discoveries and developments? [14:50]</li>\n <li>Improving upon the work that went into NeuroRacer and building the first video game therapeutic to be approved by the FDA: EndeavorRX. [18:13]</li>\n <li>Why does the mechanism behind this game prove effective in improving attention abilities in children with a wide variety of conditions including autism, depression, ADHD, and multiple sclerosis? [25:38]</li>\n <li>How does UCSF compare to its peers in the ecosystem of research within the United States? What is its focus? [29:22]</li>\n <li>Is risk-taking a critical ingredient for the enthusiasm required for scientific breakthroughs? How has Adam’s work evolved through these breakthroughs over the past decade we’ve known each other? [32:41]</li>\n <li>An important announcement about Neuroscape’s brand new division and its incoming, world-class director, and how and why it all came about so quickly — especially during a year of global pandemic. [39:08]</li>\n <li>How will Adam and Robin’s work fill in a gap that’s been thus far lacking in this type of research, and what is Adam most looking forward to exploring in this field with Neuroscape’s sophisticated resources of experience and technology at their disposal? How will their approach differ from methods that have been used in this area since the ’60s? [50:58]</li>\n <li>Just as the EndeavorRx game adapts to specific users for effectively treating a variety of conditions, does Adam foresee a way for psychedelic therapies to be customized for their patients to address seemingly disparate conditions? [1:07:02]</li>\n <li>How do we reduce the chances of a patient who is undergoing psychedelic therapy enduring a destabilizing amount of stress that causes more harm than it cures? Here’s where shamans and Adam’s closed-loop systems might mutually benefit from a knowledge exchange. [1:17:54]</li>\n <li>There’s not really one psychedelic community, but a number of tribal factions at odds with one another along the spectrum between science and superstition. In such a friction-heavy environment, why does Adam think his work has been viewed in such a positive light? [1:22:34]</li>\n <li>A request for the audience from Adam, information about how interested listeners might get involved with or support his research, and parting thoughts. scripts machines, media scripts human beings.”</p>\n <cite>— Balaji Srinivasan</cite>\n</blockquote> \n<p><strong>Balaji S. Srinivasan</strong> (<a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://twitter.com/balajis\" target=\"_blank\">@balajis</a>) is an angel investor and entrepreneur. Formerly the CTO of Coinbase and general partner at Andreessen Horowitz, he was also the co-founder of Earn.com (<a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2018/04/16/coinbase-buys-earn-com-and-makes-ceo-balaji-srinivasan-its-first-cto/\" target=\"_blank\">acquired by Coinbase</a>), Counsyl (<a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://twitter.com/balajis/status/1001277166032633856\" target=\"_blank\">acquired by Myriad</a>), Teleport (<a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://teleport.org/blog/2017/04/teleport-a-move-guides-company/\" target=\"_blank\">acquired by Topia</a>), and <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://coincenter.org/about\" target=\"_blank\">Coin Center</a>.</p> \n<p>He was named to the <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://www.technologyreview.com/lists/innovators-under-35/2013/entrepreneur/balaji-srinivasan/\" target=\"_blank\"><em>MIT Technology Review</em>’s “Innovators Under 35,”</a> won a <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://www.wsj.com/articles/SB10001424052748703470904575500353438285456\" target=\"_blank\">Wall Street Journal Innovation Award</a>, and holds a BS/MS/PhD in Electrical Engineering and an MS in Chemical Engineering, all from Stanford University. Balaji also teaches the occasional class at Stanford, including an online MOOC in 2013, which reached 250,000+ students worldwide.</p> \n<p>To learn more about Balaji’s most recent project, sign up at <a href=\"http://1729.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\"><strong>1729.com</strong></a>, a newsletter that pays you. [3:01:38]</li>\n <li>Balaji explains how a 51 percent democracy is like a Fosbury Flop, and the types of votes that <em>really</em> make a difference in such a system. [3:05:18]</li>\n <li>What a convince-oriented “crypto” government versus a coercion-focused fiat government might look like. [3:12:41]</li>\n <li>India: the dark horse, what is currently at stake as it considers banning crypto, and what Balaji sees as its way forward — by embracing crypto, learning from China’s ascendancy in the global value chain, and claiming its rightful place in the media hierarchy. [3:17:42]</li>\n <li>Parting thoughts.
